Please read the attached paper draft (and convo4 if needed for context). In the context of the W=0 open gap in the paper (check audit items, etc), please do the following 3 math tasks:

### Task 1: affine normal form audit

‚ÄúAssume a smooth planar curve in local affine coordinates satisfies (x'(0)\neq 0), (K(0)=0), and (K) changes sign. Put it into local affine normal form near the boundary and determine whether the generic model is (y=ax^3+O(x^4)). Then analyze whether tangents from one side intersect the other side, and under what extra jet conditions that fails.‚Äù

This is good because it is self-contained and may uncover exactly what extra vanishing condition would save you.

### Task 2: determinant / collinearity route at (W=0)

‚ÄúFor a local affine curve (y=ax^3+bx^4+O(x^5)), compute the three-point determinant
[
\det!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&y(x_1)\
1&x_2&y(x_2)\
1&x_3&y(x_3)
\end{pmatrix}
]
and analyze its sign for ordered triples across the inflection point. Then determine what additional jet conditions would make the determinant have fixed Vandermonde sign across the boundary.‚Äù

This directly tests the aggressive determinant route at (W=0).

### Task 3: secant/tangent obstruction search

‚ÄúConstruct or rule out local counterexamples near a generic affine inflection to the statement: ‚Äòno line can be 2-secant to two branches separated by the inflection.‚Äô Then identify what stronger geometric property would be sufficient to restore a no-4-secant theorem.‚Äù

This is useful because it may help you identify the exact strengthened theorem you actually need.

* **Task 1:** generic affine normal form and tangent crossing.
* **Task 2:** determinant sign behavior across an inflection.
* **Task 3:** local counterexamples / strengthened theorem discovery.

I‚Äôm reading the draft and the attached context together, then I‚Äôll attack the three local questions directly rather than just summarizing the gap. The main thing I want to pin down is whether the generic affine-inflection model itself already creates tangent/secant obstructions, or whether the paper‚Äôs hoped-for sign control could still survive under a stronger jet hypothesis.

I found the key context: the draft now explicitly treats generic W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundaries as the remaining geometric obstruction, and convo4 pushes exactly the fallback you‚Äôre asking about ‚Äî replacing the tangent-separator route with a determinant-sign route across the boundary. I‚Äôm now checking whether the local affine math actually supports that stronger route, or instead shows where it breaks.

I read the draft/convo context with the right lens: the paper now treats generic W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundaries as the remaining geometric obstruction, and convo4 suggests replacing the tangent-separator route by a determinant-sign route across such a boundary. The local affine math says something sharper: the tangent-separator route really does fail generically, the naive determinant fixed-sign route also fails generically, but a genuine local no-4-secant statement can still be true near a simple affine inflection.
Task 1: affine normal form audit

That means the tangent-separator route is genuinely broken at a generic W=0W=0 affine-inflection boundary, not just missing a technical lemma.

and compute

There is a standard identity:

For ordered triples x1<x2<x3x1‚Äã<x2‚Äã<x3‚Äã, the Vandermonde VV is positive. So the sign of DD is controlled to leading order by
a(x1+x2+x3).
a(x1‚Äã+x2‚Äã+x3‚Äã).

That is the decisive point. Near an inflection, the determinant does not have fixed Vandermonde sign. It flips according to the sign of the centroid x1+x2+x3x1‚Äã+x2‚Äã+x3‚Äã. For example, with Œµ>0Œµ>0,
(‚àí3Œµ,‚àíŒµ,Œµ)‚áíx1+x2+x3=‚àí3Œµ<0,
(‚àí3Œµ,‚àíŒµ,Œµ)‚áíx1‚Äã+x2‚Äã+x3‚Äã=‚àí3Œµ<0,

(‚àíŒµ,Œµ,3Œµ)‚áíx1+x2+x3=3Œµ>0.
(‚àíŒµ,Œµ,3Œµ)‚áíx1‚Äã+x2‚Äã+x3‚Äã=3Œµ>0.

So even for arbitrarily small ordered triples straddling the inflection, DD takes both signs.

For the pure cubic this is exact:
D=a‚ÄâV(x1,x2,x3)‚Äâ(x1+x2+x3).
D=aV(x1‚Äã,x2‚Äã,x3‚Äã)(x1‚Äã+x2‚Äã+x3‚Äã).

So the hoped-for ‚Äúfixed Vandermonde sign across the boundary‚Äù is false for the ordinary affine-inflection model.

That means the aggressive determinant route, at least in this naive affine form, does not survive generic W=0W=0 geometry. Convo4 floated exactly that hope; the model calculation says no.

What extra jet condition would make the determinant have fixed Vandermonde sign?

At the level of local jets, you would have to kill the cubic coefficient aa. But a‚âÝ0aÓÄÝ=0 is exactly the generic simple-inflection condition. So the fixed-sign property cannot be recovered inside the generic W=0W=0 class by a mild extra jet assumption.

And killing aa does not really solve the problem in any clean way. If the next nonzero term is quartic, then curvature does not change sign generically, so you are no longer in the inflection case. If the next nonzero term is higher odd order, you are still in an inflection-type situation, but there is no reason for the corresponding divided difference to become sign-definite on mixed-sign triples. So ‚Äúfixed Vandermonde sign‚Äù is not an ordinary local-inflection phenomenon. It would have to come from some special structure of the specific triple (c,v5,Œî7)(c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã), not from generic affine geometry.
Task 3: secant/tangent obstruction search

Here the answer splits in two.

A local counterexample to tangent separation exists immediately: for y=x3y=x3, the tangent at x=sx=s meets the opposite side again at x=‚àí2sx=‚àí2s. So any theorem claiming a one-sided support barrier across a generic affine inflection is false.

But a local counterexample to no-4-secant does not exist near a generic affine inflection.

Let
y=f(x),f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(0)‚âÝ0,
y=f(x),f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(0)ÓÄÝ=0,

with f(0)=f‚Ä≤(0)=f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(0)=0f(0)=f‚Ä≤(0)=f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(0)=0. After shrinking the neighborhood, f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤ has exactly one simple zero at 00, hence changes sign once and is strictly monotone.

Now fix any affine line y=mx+by=mx+b, and set
g(x):=f(x)‚àímx‚àíb.
g(x):=f(x)‚àímx‚àíb.

Then
g‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(x)=f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(x),
g‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(x)=f‚Ä≤‚Ä≤(x),

so g‚Ä≤‚Ä≤g‚Ä≤‚Ä≤ also changes sign exactly once. Therefore g‚Ä≤g‚Ä≤ has at most two zeros, and by Rolle‚Äôs theorem gg has at most three zeros.

So in a sufficiently small neighborhood of a generic affine inflection, every line meets the curve at most three times.

That rules out a local ‚Äú2-secant on the left plus 2-secant on the right‚Äù configuration. So the honest local picture is:

the tangent-barrier theorem fails, but the local no-4-secant theorem can still be true.

This is why the paper‚Äôs current geometric gap is subtle. The obstruction is not that generic affine inflections locally create 4-secants; it is that the old proof mechanism cannot exclude them globally.

What stronger property would be sufficient to restore a no-4-secant theorem?

The clean sufficient property is that the triple
{1,x,y}
{1,x,y}

be an extended Chebyshev system on the whole connected block under study. Equivalently, for every ordered triple x1<x2<x3x1‚Äã<x2‚Äã<x3‚Äã,
det‚Å°‚Äâ‚Å£(1x1y(x1)1x2y(x2)1x3y(x3))
det
‚Äã111‚Äãx1‚Äãx2‚Äãx3‚Äã‚Äãy(x1‚Äã)y(x2‚Äã)y(x3‚Äã)‚Äã
‚Äã

has one fixed sign times the Vandermonde sign. Under that hypothesis, no three distinct points are collinear, so a fortiori no affine line can be 4-secant.

A weaker but still sufficient condition is the one convo4 hints at: for each fixed pair s<ts<t, the function
u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)
u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)

has at most one zero on each connected component of the complement of [s,t][s,t]. That weaker ‚Äútwo-point variation‚Äù property is already enough to kill pair-pair configurations across two branches.

So my bottom line is:

For the W=0W=0 open gap, the local affine audit points in a fairly definite direction. Generic W=0W=0 boundaries really do look like ordinary affine inflections. That destroys adjacent tangent separation. It also destroys any naive fixed-sign determinant law. But it does not produce local 4-secants. So the right strengthened theorem is not a tangent-support statement and not a bare local jet statement. It has to be a genuinely stronger order-3 Chebyshev or determinant-variation property of the actual triple (c,v5,Œî7)(c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã), if such a property is true at all.

If you want, the next thing I‚Äôd do is turn this into ‚Äúpaper consequences‚Äù: exactly which current conjectural routes are dead, which remain viable, and what the clean honest theorem statement should now be.

ok give a summary of paper consequences

I‚Äôve got the local affine conclusions. I‚Äôm now mapping them back onto the paper‚Äôs actual architecture so I can say which parts survive unchanged, which need downgrading, and what the honest replacement theorem would look like.

Here is the clean paper-level consequence summary.

The big consequence is that the paper‚Äôs current endgame has to bifurcate. The draft/convo currently treats ‚Äúadjacent tangent-separator sign regularity ‚áí‚áí global no-4-secant ‚áí‚áí no bad core‚Äù as the main remaining bridge, and it even states an adjacent theorem under generic boundary hypotheses saying tangent lines from the right interval do not meet the adjacent left interval. But the local affine-inflection audit shows that at a generic W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary, the affine normal form is y=ax3+O(x4)y=ax3+O(x4), and in that model tangents from one side do hit the other side. So that theorem cannot be correct in that stated generality.

So the first concrete consequence is:

1. The generic W=0W=0 version of the adjacent tangent-separator theorem has to be withdrawn, weakened, or made conditional.
Not ‚Äúneeds a tighter proof.‚Äù The local model says the claimed geometric statement is generically false. In paper terms, the W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 case cannot be handled by the same tangent-support barrier presently claimed for generic boundaries. That means the current route
generic boundary hypotheses‚áíadjacent tangent-separator sign regularity
generic boundary hypotheses‚áíadjacent tangent-separator sign regularity

is not salvageable as written.

The second consequence is more nuanced:

2. The pure determinant globalization route also does not close the W=0W=0 case.
Convo4 already suspected this and explicitly says the aggressive determinant attack works across M=0M=0 turning-point boundaries but fails in general across inflection-type W=0W=0 boundaries. The affine determinant computation confirms that: for
y=ax3+bx4+O(x5),
y=ax3+bx4+O(x5),

the ordered-triple determinant is Vandermonde times a factor whose leading term is a(x1+x2+x3)a(x1‚Äã+x2‚Äã+x3‚Äã), so the sign flips on triples straddling the inflection. Thus there is no generic fixed-sign determinant law across a W=0W=0 boundary.

That means the paper should not present a uniform determinant-sign replacement for the whole endgame. At best, determinant sign regularity is part of the M=0M=0 / turning-point story, not the generic W=0W=0 story. That is exactly the split convo4 was already converging toward.

The third consequence is the most important positive one:

3. The W=0W=0 gap is narrower than ‚Äúlocal 4-secant chaos.‚Äù
The local affine-inflection model kills tangent separation, but it does not create local 4-secants. Near a simple affine inflection, any line meets the curve at most three times. So the paper‚Äôs hoped-for global no-4-secant statement is not refuted by local geometry; only the current proof mechanism is. This is why the endgame is still alive in principle: the obstruction is proof-theoretic, not an outright local counterexample to no-4-secant.

In other words, the paper should now say something like: generic W=0W=0 boundaries are not forbidden because of local multi-secant explosion; they are hard because the current tangent-barrier and determinant-sign tools do not control them.

From that, the next architectural consequence follows:

4. Two-pair rigidity and minimal bad-core exclusion are no longer ‚Äúalmost done from adjacent tangent separation.‚Äù
Convo4 had been treating a strong adjacent theorem as the one statement that would essentially collapse two-pair rigidity and minimal bad-core exclusion. After the affine audit, that is too optimistic. Those sections can no longer rely on generic adjacent tangent-separator sign regularity at W=0W=0. So either:

    those later sections must be downgraded to conditional on a stronger cross-boundary hypothesis, or

    they need a genuinely different geometric input for the W=0W=0 case.

The cleanest candidate input is not ‚Äúendpoint tangent does not meet the other side,‚Äù because that is generically false. It is something more like a third-order Chebyshev / collinearity-control property for the actual triple (c,v5,Œî7)(c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã), if such a property can be proved.

So the honest update to the roadmap is:

5. The real remaining theorem is now more specialized and more intrinsic.
For M=0M=0 boundaries, the determinant/tangent-slope picture may still be essentially under control, as convo4 suggests. For W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0, the battlefield is no longer tangent support. The viable target is some stronger property of the specific normalized curve
Œì(h)=(v5(h)c(h),Œî7(h)c(h))
Œì(h)=(c(h)v5‚Äã(h)‚Äã,c(h)Œî7‚Äã(h)‚Äã)

or equivalently of the triple (c,v5,Œî7)(c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã), such as a restricted determinant-variation law or ECT-type order-3 property strong enough to prevent pair-pair secancy without claiming tangent separation. That matches the draft/convo‚Äôs own emphasis that the kernel
K(s,t)=det‚Å°(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t))
K(s,t)=det(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t))

is the native object, but it means the needed theorem is subtler than the one currently stated.

So, stripped to essentials, the paper consequences are:

    the current generic W=0W=0 tangent-separator theorem is not believable as stated and should not remain unconditional;

    the pure determinant route does not generically fix W=0W=0;

    the endgame is still viable in principle because local W=0W=0 geometry does not produce local 4-secants;

    but the remaining theorem is now a genuinely different W=0W=0-specific geometric rigidity statement, not the current tangent-support claim.

The clean editorial consequence is to explicitly split the endgame into two boundary types:
M=0vs.W=0, M‚âÝ0,
M=0vs.W=0, MÓÄÝ=0,

and state plainly that only the second is still open. Convo4 was already moving in that direction; the affine audit makes that split essentially mandatory.

The clean mathematical consequence is that the next attack should not be ‚Äúprove the adjacent tangent theorem harder.‚Äù It should be ‚Äúfind the correct W=0W=0 replacement theorem.‚Äù

check this latest draft for new W=0 work

I‚Äôm checking whether the new draft actually adds a viable W=0W=0 argument, or just reframes the same open gap. I‚Äôll focus on what changed around the boundary-case split, any new determinant/ECT statements, and whether the draft now has an honest theorem in place of the old tangent-separator claim.

I found a real structural change: the new draft now explicitly splits the endgame into turning-boundary work that is treated as conditional/partial, and a separate W=0W=0 obstruction section that is described as unresolved. I‚Äôm reading those exact statements now to see whether the new W=0W=0 material is mathematically substantive, or mainly an honest reframing.

Yes. The draft has real new W=0W=0 work, but it is mostly a successful reframing and localization of the obstruction, not a solution of it.

The biggest improvement is that the paper is now much more honest about where the geometry breaks. It no longer pretends to have one generic adjacent-boundary theorem covering both M=0M=0 and W=0W=0. Instead, it splits the cases: turning boundaries
M(hb)=0,M‚Ä≤(hb)‚âÝ0,N(hb)‚âÝ0
M(hb‚Äã)=0,M‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0,N(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0

get a conditional adjacent tangent-separator theorem, while for
W(hb)=0,M(hb)‚âÝ0
W(hb‚Äã)=0,M(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0

the draft explicitly says no adjacent tangent-separation statement is asserted, and identifies the local affine jet as cubic-inflection type unless further structure forces W‚Ä≤(hb)=0W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)=0. That is a real upgrade in correctness.

What is genuinely new for W=0W=0 is this.

First, the draft now records the exact local jet computation in the normalized chart
x=v5c,y=Œî7c,
x=cv5‚Äã‚Äã,y=cŒî7‚Äã‚Äã,

namely
d2ydx2‚à£hb=0,d3ydx3‚à£hb=c(hb)5M(hb)4W‚Ä≤(hb),

‚Äãhb‚Äã‚Äã=0,dx3d3y‚Äã
‚Äãhb‚Äã‚Äã=M(hb‚Äã)4c(hb‚Äã)5‚ÄãW‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã),

so the local model is
y=c(hb)5W‚Ä≤(hb)6M(hb)4x3+O(x4).
y=6M(hb‚Äã)4c(hb‚Äã)5W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)‚Äãx3+O(x4).

That pins the obstruction to one scalar: W‚Ä≤(hb)W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã). This is the cleanest formulation the paper has had so far.

Second, the draft adds the exact identities
W=det‚Å°(F,F‚Ä≤,F‚Ä≤‚Ä≤),W‚Ä≤=det‚Å°(F,F‚Ä≤,F‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤),
W=det(F,F‚Ä≤,F‚Ä≤‚Ä≤),W‚Ä≤=det(F,F‚Ä≤,F‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤),

with explicit expansions showing how WW and W‚Ä≤W‚Ä≤ depend on c,v5,Œî7c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã and derivatives. That is important because it supports the paper‚Äôs new claim that the highest genuinely new jet entering the W=0W=0 obstruction is still governed by the order-7 package through Œî7Œî7‚Äã, not by some brand-new primitive order-9 invariant. Conceptually, that is the strongest new W=0W=0 point in the draft.

Third, the global geometry has been reorganized around that split. The adjacent tangent-separator theorem is now explicitly only for turning boundaries, the global no-secant theorem is correspondingly weakened to a partial theorem on turning-boundary generic blocks, and the later remarks say plainly that the main unresolved global issue is now the W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary. That is a substantial improvement over the older architecture, where the W=0W=0 failure mode was still partly buried inside a supposedly generic adjacent theorem.

So the good news is: the new draft does appear to incorporate the right conceptual repair from the recent discussion. Convo4 was pushing exactly this kind of change ‚Äî isolate W=0W=0 as the remaining obstruction instead of silently treating it as another generic boundary case ‚Äî and the current draft now does that.

But the important negative conclusion is just as clear:

the draft still does not have new W=0W=0 mathematics that closes the gap.

It does not prove W‚Ä≤(hb)=0W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)=0.
It does not prove any W=0W=0-specific replacement theorem for tangent separation.
It does not prove a determinant-sign theorem across W=0W=0.
It does not prove a W=0W=0-specific no-4-secant theorem.

What it has now is a good diagnosis:

    generic W=0W=0 looks like affine inflection,

    affine inflection kills tangent-separator sign regularity,

    the obstruction is encoded through W‚Ä≤(hb)W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã),

    and W‚Ä≤(hb)W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã) is algebraically tied to the septic package.

That is meaningful progress, but still diagnosis, not cure. The draft itself says this repeatedly in the new remarks on the ‚ÄúW=0W=0 obstruction,‚Äù ‚Äúcurrent geometric bottleneck,‚Äù and ‚Äúcurrent state of the argument.‚Äù

My bottom-line assessment:

The new W=0W=0 work is good and worth keeping. It makes the paper more honest and more sharply focused. It narrows the remaining issue to a definite local-global theorem about the actual triple (c,v5,Œî7)(c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã), with W‚Ä≤(hb)W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã) as the local scalar bottleneck. That is real progress.

But it is still an open-gap package, not a closure package.

There is one further editorial consequence you should probably act on: because the draft now openly says the main unresolved global issue is W=0W=0, the later ‚ÄúFinal contradiction‚Äù framing reads too strong unless it is explicitly limited to the pair-like / turning-boundary-controlled branch. As it stands, the WIP remark there still talks about an incomplete endgame, but the section title and opening sentence still sound like the proof globally closes. That now clashes more sharply with the new W=0W=0 honesty than it did before.

So, in one sentence:

The new W=0W=0 work is a successful audit repair and architectural cleanup, but not yet a new theorem.

If you want, I can next give you a very targeted referee-style verdict: ‚Äúwhat is now honest, what is still overstated, and the exact theorem statement the paper should downgrade to today.‚Äù

Yes. At this point I think there are only two serious endgames left for the W=0W=0 attack, and one of them is much more promising than the other.

The current draft/convo already has the right reduction: at a boundary with

So the live fork is:

My honest judgment is that Route B is more promising, and Route A should now be treated as a sharp diagnostic computation rather than the main hope.

Why I say that: the local affine audit already showed that generic W=0W=0 looks like
y=ax3+O(x4),
y=ax3+O(x4),

or more modestly the ‚Äútwo-point variation‚Äù statement that for fixed s<ts<t, the function u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) has at most one zero on each connected component of the complement of [s,t][s,t]. Convo4 is right that this would already kill pair-pair configurations.

So here is how I would continue the attack.

First, do the short decisive computation on Route A before spending more emotional energy on it.

You now have
W‚Ä≤=M‚ÄâŒî7‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤+(v5c‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚àícv5‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤)‚ÄâŒî7‚Ä≤+(c‚Ä≤v5‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚àív5‚Ä≤c‚Ä≤‚Ä≤‚Ä≤)‚ÄâŒî7.

And the draft/convo already says the highest genuinely new contribution is governed by the weight-one septic slice of Œî7Œî7‚Äã. So the right calculation is not ‚Äúprove W‚Ä≤=0W‚Ä≤=0 abstractly.‚Äù It is:

That calculation has only two possible outcomes.

Either the top new contribution to W‚Ä≤W‚Ä≤ factors by the boundary equation or otherwise vanishes identically there. Then Route A is alive and you have a real shot at proving nongeneric jet behavior.

Or it comes out generically nonzero. Then Route A is dead, and you should stop trying to force W‚Ä≤(hb)=0W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)=0. That is still valuable, because it would tell you quickly that the proof must go by Route B instead. This is the best ‚Äúgo / no-go‚Äù calculation now available.

But I would not make Route A the main front, because even if the top new slice looks favorable, you still then need a real structural reason that the full W‚Ä≤W‚Ä≤ vanishes on the entire W=0W=0 locus. That is a strong target.

The more promising front is Route B, and I would break it into two theorem-sized pieces.

The first piece is a local simple-W=0W=0 determinant theorem.

In the affine-inflection model
y=ax3+bx4+O(x5),

the determinant for ordered triples has the form

That is the place where I would seriously consider changing formalism. So the concrete priority order I‚Äôd use is:

4. Only after that, return to minimal bad-core / final contradiction.
Trying to finish the endgame before one of those two W=0W=0 theorems is in hand will just create more conditional prose.

So my blunt answer is:

Stronger statement: there is actually a unique opposite-side zero

You can get a bit more.

with ‚àÇuH=a+O(Œµ)‚âÝ0‚àÇu‚ÄãH=a+O(Œµ)ÓÄÝ=0. So by the implicit function theorem there is a unique smooth root
u‚àó(x1,x2)=‚àí(x1+x2)+O(Œµ2).
u‚àó‚Äã(x1‚Äã,x2‚Äã)=‚àí(x1‚Äã+x2‚Äã)+O(Œµ2).

Since x1,x2<0x1‚Äã,x2‚Äã<0, this root lies on the opposite side for ŒµŒµ small.

So near a simple W=0W=0 boundary, the truth is not ‚Äúno opposite-side determinant zero.‚Äù The truth is:

    there is generically one opposite-side collinearity for each nearby same-side pair,

    and there are not two.

That is exactly the kind of behavior compatible with an affine inflection.
What this buys you for the paper

This is a real theorem, not just a reformulation.

It shows that a simple W=0W=0 boundary with W‚Ä≤(hb)‚âÝ0W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0 is locally determinant-benign: it does not create the kind of repeated opposite-side collinearity that would feed a local pair-pair / 4-secant obstruction. The bad news about W=0W=0 was that tangent separation fails generically; the good news is that the determinant still has controlled one-dimensional behavior on the opposite side. That is precisely the direction convo4 was suggesting with the two-point variation target.

So the proof attack now sharpens to:

    keep the current W‚Ä≤W‚Ä≤ reduction, but use it to certify the simple-inflection normal form rather than to force W‚Ä≤(hb)=0W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)=0;

    insert the local theorem above;

    then try to propagate this local one-zero-per-side control along interval chains.

That last propagation step is still open. The theorem above only handles pairs s<ts<t that are themselves close to the simple W=0W=0 boundary. It does not yet prove the full global statement
u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) has at most one zero on each component of R‚àñ[s,t]
u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) has at most one zero on each component of R‚àñ[s,t]

for arbitrary fixed s<ts<t. But it does prove that the simple W=0W=0 boundary is not the place where local repeated determinant zeros are born.

That is the cleanest mathematical gain available from the current W‚Ä≤W‚Ä≤ push.

The next thing I‚Äôd do is write this up in paper notation as a proposition right after the W/W‚Ä≤W/W‚Ä≤ identities and the cubic-inflection coefficient formula.

continue the attack

I‚Äôm pushing past the local theorem now. The next real question is whether that local one-zero-per-side result can be turned into a global pair-pair exclusion mechanism, or whether there‚Äôs another hidden place repeated zeros can re-enter.

Feedback from the other chat: This is actually good.

I think that local theorem is **mathematically real** and worth keeping. The proof in the pasted note is the right one: pass to the affine chart
[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},\qquad y=\frac{\Delta_7}{c},
]
use (M(h_b)\neq 0) to take (x) as a local parameter, normalize to
[
f(0)=f'(0)=0,\qquad f(x)=a x^3+b x^4+O(x^5),\ a\neq 0,
]
and then factor the three-point determinant as a Vandermonde times the second divided difference
[
f[x_1,x_2,u].
]
For a cubic-inflection jet, that divided difference is affine in (u) to leading order, with derivative (a+O(\rho)), so it is strictly monotone on the opposite side. That really does give ‚Äúat most one opposite-side zero,‚Äù and in fact a unique one for nearby same-side pairs.

So I would treat the pasted result as a **new local theorem**, not just heuristic commentary.

The important consequence is also exactly what the other chat says: a simple boundary
[
W(h_b)=0,\qquad M(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad W'(h_b)\neq 0
]
is not a place where **two** opposite-side determinant zeros are born. Locally, it behaves like an ordinary affine inflection: one opposite-side collinearity per nearby same-side pair, not two. That means the old attack ‚Äúforce (W'(h_b)=0)‚Äù is no longer the only viable route. A second route is now open:

**accept generic simple (W=0) inflection, and prove it is locally pair-pair sterile.**

That is a real strategic shift.

What it does **not** do is finish the global theorem by itself. The note already says that honestly: the theorem is local in the regime where (s,t) are themselves close to the simple (W=0) boundary, and it does not yet prove a full global statement like
[
u\mapsto D(s,t,u)
]
has at most one zero on each component of (\mathbb R\setminus[s,t]) for arbitrary fixed (s<t). So it kills local pair-pair birth at simple (W=0), but it does not globalize automatically. 

That said, I think it changes the main attack in a useful way.

Instead of trying to prove
[
W'(h_b)=0
]
at every (W=0,\ M\neq0) boundary, I would now split the (W=0) analysis into two cases:

1. **simple (W=0)**: (W'(h_b)\neq 0).
   Use the new local determinant theorem to show this case is benign for pair-pair / repeated opposite-side zeros.

2. **multiple (W=0)**: (W'(h_b)=0).
   This becomes the only genuinely dangerous (W=0) case, and that is where the order-(7) algebra should still be pushed.

That is much sharper than the current ‚Äúall (W=0) is an obstruction‚Äù picture. The simple case is no longer a full obstruction; it is a controlled local phenomenon.

So the next exact attack I would make is:

First, insert this as a proposition right after the (W/W') identities and cubic-inflection formula. It belongs there conceptually, because it is the first theorem that turns the (W')-analysis into geometric content. The current draft already isolates the simple (W=0) affine-inflection model but does not yet exploit it in determinant form.

Second, add the corollary you really want:

> **Corollary.** A simple (W=0,\ M\neq0) boundary cannot support a local pair-pair configuration across the two adjacent sides.

That is the real payload for the proof. It says: near such a boundary, a line through two same-side points can hit the other side at most once. So the dangerous ‚Äútwo points on each side‚Äù configuration cannot be created locally there. This is the local geometric fact the draft currently lacks.

Third, reformulate the global remaining issue accordingly:

> the only (W=0) boundaries that can still threaten pair-pair birth are **multiple** (W)-zeros.

That is a much cleaner bottleneck than the current blanket (W=0) audit remark.

Fourth, then the order-(7) push gets a better target. You no longer need the septic package to kill **all** (W=0) boundaries. You only need it to control the multiple-zero locus
[
W=0,\qquad W'=0,\qquad M\neq 0.
]
That is a much narrower algebraic target.

So my recommendation is:

* **Yes, keep this theorem.**
* **Yes, pivot the attack around it.**
* Use it to declare simple (W=0) locally safe.
* Then concentrate the remaining order-(7) work on the multiple-(W)-zero case.

That is a real improvement in the proof strategy, not just a side lemma.

I agree with that feedback, and I think we can now sharpen the attack further.

2. Consequence for W=0W=0 boundaries

Now apply this to the actual curve in the paper.

    Corollary. Let hbhb‚Äã satisfy c(hb)‚âÝ0c(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0, M(hb)‚âÝ0M(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0, W(hb)=0W(hb‚Äã)=0, and assume WW changes sign across hbhb‚Äã. That is better than the simple-vs-multiple split.
3. What this changes strategically

This means the proof no longer needs the order-7 package to kill local pair-pair birth at W=0W=0 boundaries.

That local problem is now gone.

The remaining W=0W=0 issue is therefore not:
‚Äúcan a pair-pair configuration be born near such a boundary?‚Äù

It is:
‚Äúcan a single determinant-zero branch be transported nonlocally across several intervals and come back as a second opposite-side zero somewhere else?‚Äù

That is a much more global question.

So the real remaining battlefield becomes:

    local sterility at W=0W=0 ‚Äî now essentially solved;

    global propagation / branching of zeros of
    u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)=det‚Å°(F(s),F(t),F(u));
    u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)=det(F(s),F(t),F(u));

    turning-boundary transport, where the current draft still carries the zero-capture vulnerability.

In particular, the phrase ‚Äúall W=0W=0 is an obstruction‚Äù is now too coarse. The honest bottleneck is narrower:

    W=0W=0 is not a local pair-pair birthplace;

    the unresolved issue is whether zeros of the determinant can be continued or accumulated globally across interval chains.

4. The next theorem to attack

The next serious target is no longer ‚Äúprove W‚Ä≤(hb)=0W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)=0‚Äù and not even ‚Äúsplit simple vs multiple W=0W=0.‚Äù

It is this continuation theorem:

    For fixed s<ts<t, the zero set of
    u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)
    u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)

    cannot branch into two opposite-side zeros when uu passes through a sign-changing W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary.

Locally, we have essentially proved that already: near such a boundary, the zero set is one-dimensional and single-valued because the opposite-side zero, if present, is unique.

So the real work left is to globalize that uniqueness. The line of attack I would use now is:

    prove a local implicit-function continuation lemma for the unique zero branch across a W=0W=0 boundary;

    then show any true pair-pair configuration would have to be created or destroyed at a turning boundary instead;

    then push the turning-boundary argument, where the current draft already has the right formal theorem stack but still depends on zero-capture.

So the attack has shifted again, and in a good way:

W=0W=0 is no longer the place where double opposite-side zeros are born.
The remaining problem is global continuation, plus the turning-boundary zero-capture gap.

That is a much tighter endgame than before.

If you want, the next step I‚Äôd take is to write the continuation lemma precisely in (s,t,u)(s,t,u)-space and see whether the local uniqueness can be turned into a genuine global ‚Äúno branching across W=0W=0‚Äù statement.

What this really gives you

This is stronger than ‚Äúsimple W=0W=0 is locally safe.‚Äù It says:

At any sign-changing W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary, repeated opposite-side zeros of u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) cannot be born by local branching.

So an inflection-type W=0W=0 boundary is not a local pair-pair birthplace. That lines up with the draft‚Äôs current shift away from tangent-separator language and toward determinant variation.
What still remains

This does not yet prove the full two-point variation theorem from convo4:
u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) has at most one zero on each component of R‚àñ[s,t]

for arbitrary fixed s<ts<t. That stronger global theorem is still the real target.

What the new theorem does prove is narrower and very useful:

    a second opposite-side zero cannot be created locally at a sign-changing W=0W=0 boundary;

    if a global pair-pair configuration exists, its ‚Äúbirth/death‚Äù mechanism must come from somewhere else.

Given the current draft, that shifts the live bottleneck back toward the turning-boundary/global-transport side, which is exactly where the present partial global no-secant theorem still sits.
The next exact attack

The next theorem to try is now:

    Transport theorem. Fix s<ts<t. Along a chain of adjacent ECT intervals, the zero set of u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) cannot gain an extra branch when crossing a sign-changing W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary.

The local no-branching theorem above is the hard local input for that. What remains is the chain argument.

The clean way to attack that is:

    define the zero set
    Zs,t:={u: D(s,t,u)=0};
    Zs,t‚Äã:={u: D(s,t,u)=0};

    show that on each ECT interval, Zs,tZs,t‚Äã is discrete by the ECT property of (c,v5,Œî7)(c,v5‚Äã,Œî7‚Äã) when c,M,W‚âÝ0c,M,WÓÄÝ=0;

    use the local no-branching theorem to show Zs,tZs,t‚Äã cannot gain multiplicity across a sign-changing W=0W=0 boundary;

    conclude that any genuine gain of a second opposite-side zero must occur at a turning boundary, not at W=0W=0.

That is the next front I would push.

Why this matters strategically

This changes the proof attack materially.

The draft currently still treats W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 as the main unresolved global issue, while the turning-boundary stack is already isolated separately and the remaining mismatch there is the zero-capture hypothesis.

But the theorem above says:

finite-order W=0W=0 boundaries are locally harmless for pair-pair creation.

So the remaining global danger is no longer ‚Äúgeneric W=0W=0 inflection behavior‚Äù as such. It is narrower:

    the unresolved turning-boundary / zero-capture mechanism, or

    some genuinely nonlocal continuation phenomenon, or

    pathological WW-flatness beyond finite order.

If the ambient functions are analytic, then isolated zeros are automatically finite-order unless WW vanishes identically on a neighborhood. In that analytic setting, the local W=0W=0 obstruction is essentially gone.
The next exact attack

I would now attack this reduction theorem:

    Reduction target. Assume WW is analytic and not identically zero on any interval. Then no local pair-pair configuration can be born at a W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary. Consequently any minimal global pair-pair obstruction must be created at a turning boundary M=0M=0, not at a W=0W=0 boundary.

That is not quite fully proved yet, because ‚Äúcreated‚Äù is a global statement about zero-branch continuation, not only local geometry. But the local half is now in hand.

So the immediate next step is to turn the argument above into a formal proposition in the draft, right after the W=0W=0 affine-chart remark. Then the next theorem to prove is the continuation/reduction statement that moves the remaining burden back to turning boundaries and zero-capture.

That is the strongest clean attack I can see now, and I think it is real.

attack

Immediate payoff

On any connected interval JJ where WW has fixed nonzero sign, every ordered triple s<t<us<t<u in JJ satisfies
sgn‚Å°D(s,t,u)=sgn‚Å°W‚à£J.

That is stronger than the infinitesimal ECT statement already in the draft. The ECT proposition says a line meets the curve at most twice on such an interval; this theorem upgrades that to a discrete sign-regularity law for every ordered triple in the interval.

So you now get, on each WW-sign interval:

    no three ordered points are collinear;

    for fixed s<ts<t in that interval, u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) has fixed sign for u>tu>t still in the same interval, and the opposite fixed sign for u<su<s still in the same interval;

    in particular, no line can be 22-secant twice inside a single WW-sign interval.

That is a genuine new theorem for the paper.
How this combines with the W=0W=0 local theorem

You already have the local finite-order W=0W=0 sterility attack: at a W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary, the affine chart gives a finite-order inflection model, and a fixed same-side pair produces at most one opposite-side zero locally. So finite-order W=0W=0 boundaries are not local pair-pair birthplaces.

Now add the determinant mean-value theorem above. Then the geometry is much tighter:

    inside each WW-sign interval, discrete sign regularity prevents any internal oscillation of DD;

    across a finite-order W=0W=0 boundary, local inflection theory prevents a zero branch from splitting into two.

So a second opposite-side zero branch cannot be born inside a WW-sign interval and cannot be born locally at a finite-order W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary.

That leaves only two serious mechanisms:

    a turning boundary M=0M=0, where the draft still relies on the conditional adjacent tangent theorem and zero-capture, or

    some pathological WW-flatness if analyticity is not being used.

The draft/convo already says the turning-boundary theorem is the remaining conditional geometric input, and that the current partial global no-secant theorem still depends on it.
So what did we just reduce?

Quite a lot.

Before, the global obstruction was ‚ÄúW=0W=0 might ruin the whole determinant picture.‚Äù

After this attack, the picture is:

    on every open component where W‚âÝ0WÓÄÝ=0, DD has exact Vandermonde sign control by the mean-value theorem;

    at every finite-order W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary, local no-branching blocks pair-pair birth;

    therefore the only place a second determinant-zero branch can still enter is a turning boundary, unless WW is infinitely flat.

That is a real reduction of the endgame.
The next exact theorem

The next theorem to prove is now much cleaner:

    Turning-boundary birth theorem.
    Fix s<ts<t. A second zero branch of u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u)u‚Ü¶D(s,t,u) can only be created or destroyed at a turning boundary M=0M=0.

Once that is in place, the remaining job is to exclude that turning-boundary birth mechanism. And that is exactly where the current draft‚Äôs conditional tangent/zero-capture stack already lives.

So this is the attack I would make now:

    insert the determinant mean-value theorem and its corollary on each WW-sign interval;

    combine it with the local W=0W=0 inflection theorem to state a reduction lemma: finite-order W=0W=0 boundaries are sterile for pair-pair birth;

    rewrite the ‚Äúcurrent bottleneck‚Äù remark so it no longer says generic W=0W=0 is the main obstruction; the real remaining obstruction becomes turning-boundary birth / zero-capture.

That is the strongest real advance I can see from here, and unlike the old tangent route, it is using special structure the triple actually has.

continue attack

That theorem has two immediate consequences.

    not inside a fixed-sign WW-interval, by the sign-regularity theorem;

    not at a finite-order W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary, by the local inflection theorem.

or else at some pathological infinitely-flat WW-zero. In the analytic setting, the latter disappears unless WW vanishes identically nearby. Yes. Here is the clean summary of the **other thread** and of what I‚Äôve been attacking/proving since the last paper draft.

The biggest change is strategic. The geometry is no longer being treated as ‚Äúone generic adjacent-boundary theorem plus convexity.‚Äù The work since the last draft has split the problem into three distinct layers:

1. the **direct septic / order-7 algebra** for the second residual determinant (\Delta_7);
2. the **(W=0,\ M\neq 0)** local geometry of the normalized curve
   [
   \Gamma(h)=\left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}\right);
   ]
3. the **global determinant kernel**
   [
   D(s,t,u)=\det(F(s),F(t),F(u)),\qquad F=(c,v_5,\Delta_7).
   ]
   That is a real reorganization of the proof architecture, not just editorial cleanup.

What has actually been proved on the algebraic side is this. The direct (q^{(7)})-driven septic (K_1)-transport slice has been isolated, shown to be (I)-directional, and shown to feed (\Delta_7) by
[
\Delta_7^{(q^{(7)})}=u_7^{(q^{(7)})}v_5.
]
More concretely,
[
v_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}=0,\qquad
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}
=====================

\kappa\Bigl((x_2-x_1)\nu_6^{(q^{(7)})}+v(\gamma_5-\alpha_5)^{(q^{(7)})}\Bigr),
]
so the highest new direct septic contribution is already reduced to a single scalar multiplying (v_5).

That direct septic witness is not merely isolated; its two possible channels have been compared and shown **not** to cancel. In the minimal two-parameter model carrying the ((K_1,\eta_2,q^{(7)})) grading, the combined coefficient is generically nonzero, so
[
u_{7,K_1}^{(q^{(7)})}\not\equiv 0
]
on the generic one-pair region. This is one of the most important concrete advances since the last draft, because it means the order-7 package already has a real surviving direct witness.

What is **not** yet closed on the algebraic side is the full total order-7 fixed-sector pair ((u_7,v_7)). The direct (K_1) contribution is now explicit, but the draft/convo still says the total septic fixed-sector coefficient after all order-7 sectors are included is not yet known in full explicit form. So the genuine algebraic status is:

* direct highest-new / direct (q^{(7)}) slice: **isolated and generically nonzero**;
* full total septic coefficient: **still incomplete**.

On the (W=0) side, the main local advance was the exact identification of the obstruction. At a boundary with
[
c(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad M(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad W(h_b)=0,
]
the normalized curve in the affine chart has
[
\left.\frac{d^2y}{dx^2}\right|*{h_b}=0,
\qquad
\left.\frac{d^3y}{dx^3}\right|*{h_b}\propto W'(h_b),
]
so the generic local model is an ordinary affine inflection when (W'(h_b)\neq 0). The important conceptual conclusion was: nothing visible in the current (3/5/7) package forces (W'(h_b)=0), so the old ‚Äúgeneric tangent-separator theorem across (W=0)‚Äù is no longer believable. That was a real correction to the proof architecture.

But the other thread then found something stronger and more useful than trying to prove (W'(h_b)=0): a **local determinant theorem** at finite-order (W=0) boundaries. The argument is to write the normalized curve locally as a graph (y=f(x)), use
[
f''(x)\sim \lambda x^r
]
when (W) has a zero of finite order (r), and factor the three-point determinant through the second divided difference
[
H_{x_1,x_2}(u)=f[x_1,x_2,u].
]
Then:

* if (r) is even, (H) has fixed sign, so there is **no** opposite-side zero;
* if (r) is odd, (\partial_uH) has fixed sign, so there is **at most one** opposite-side zero.

So no finite-order (W=0,\ M\neq 0) boundary can support a **local pair-pair birth**. This is stronger than the earlier simple-(W'\neq 0) theorem and is probably the most important geometric theorem found since the last draft.

That local theorem materially changes the strategic picture. It means the (W=0) case should no longer be viewed as ‚Äúthe main unresolved geometry‚Äù in bulk. More precisely:

* isolated finite-order (W=0) boundaries are now **locally sterile** for pair-pair creation;
* the remaining (W=0) danger is only pathological flatness, like (W\equiv 0) on an interval or infinite-order vanishing. 

That is exactly where my (\lambda)-attack came in. Once the other thread handled finite-order (W=0), the only remaining job for the order-7 algebra was to rule out **(W)-flatness**. The clean reduction is:

if (W\equiv 0) on an open interval with (c\neq 0) and (M\neq 0), then the normalized curve has zero curvature there, hence
[
\frac{\Delta_7}{c}=A\frac{v_5}{c}+B,
]
equivalently
[
\Delta_7=A,v_5+B,c
]
on that interval. But Proposition 12.30 in the latest draft already excludes such an affine dependence under the direct (q^{(7)})-nonvanishing hypothesis. So the (\lambda)-attack has effectively proved the right thing:

[
W\not\equiv 0
]
on any connected open interval where (c\neq 0) and (M\neq 0), assuming the direct highest-new slice is generically nonzero. In other words, the order-7 algebra does not need to force (W'(h_b)=0); it suffices to rule out (W)-flatness, and that is the natural complementary job to the other thread‚Äôs finite-order theorem.

There was also a strategic global shift. The other thread pushed the idea that the real special object is the determinant kernel
[
D(s,t,u)=\det(F(s),F(t),F(u)).
]
The aggressive proposed theorem is a determinant mean-value formula of the form
[
D(s,t,u)=\frac12,W(\xi),(t-s)(u-s)(u-t)
]
for some intermediate (\xi). If true, that would immediately promote local ECT/curvature information into **discrete order-3 sign regularity** on any interval where (W) keeps sign, which is far stronger than the old support-interval or tangent-separator route. This theorem is not yet part of the paper as proved, but it is now the most promising global replacement for the failed generic tangent route.

So, since the last draft, the proof state has improved in four concrete ways.

First, the direct septic witness at order 7 is now isolated and generically nonzero.

Second, the (W=0,\ M\neq 0) obstruction has been **correctly localized**: generic local model is affine inflection, not tangent-separator sign regularity.

Third, finite-order (W=0) boundaries are now **locally harmless** for pair-pair birth. 

Fourth, the Œª-attack now naturally excludes the remaining pathological (W\equiv0) interval scenario, assuming the direct highest-new slice stays nonzero.

What remains open after all this is much narrower than before.

The full total order-7 fixed-sector coefficient is still not closed.

The global determinant mean-value theorem is still a proposed attack, not yet a theorem in the draft.

The current partial global no-secant theorem still rests on the turning-boundary / adjacent-support route and does not yet incorporate the stronger determinant-kernel program. 

And the real remaining geometric birth mechanism, if the new local (W=0) theorems are trusted, has been pushed back to **turning boundaries (M=0)** and the zero-capture / continuation problem there.

So the shortest honest summary is:

* **proved / essentially proved since the last draft:** direct septic (q^{(7)}) witness survives; (W=0,\ M\neq 0) reduces to affine-inflection geometry; finite-order (W=0) boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth; (W\equiv 0) intervals are excluded by the highest-new slice plus affine-dependence contradiction.

* **new main strategic direction:** stop trying to prove a generic tangent theorem across (W=0); instead attack the determinant kernel (D(s,t,u)) directly and reduce the global problem to turning-boundary birth / zero-capture.

New local theorem: support ordering at a generic turning boundary

Let hbhb‚Äã be a generic turning boundary:

c(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0,M(hb‚Äã)=0,M‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0,N(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0.

Let I1<I2I1‚Äã<I2‚Äã be the two adjacent parameter intervals meeting at hbhb‚Äã. For each finite slope m‚ààRm‚ààR, define the support function
œïm(h):=y(h)‚àím‚Äâx(h)=Œî7(h)‚àímv5(h)c(h).
œïm‚Äã(h):=y(h)‚àímx(h)=c(h)Œî7‚Äã(h)‚àímv5‚Äã(h)‚Äã.

Then there is a neighborhood UU of hbhb‚Äã such that, for every fixed finite mm,

    œïmœïm‚Äã is strictly monotone on UU,

    the one-sided images œïm(I1‚à©U)œïm‚Äã(I1‚Äã‚à©U) and œïm(I2‚à©U)œïm‚Äã(I2‚Äã‚à©U) are disjoint open intervals,

    their closures meet only at the common boundary value œïm(hb)œïm‚Äã(hb‚Äã).

So across a generic turning boundary, fixed-slope support intervals are locally ordered automatically, without any zero-capture argument.
Proof

Differentiate:
œïm‚Ä≤(h)=y‚Ä≤(h)‚àímx‚Ä≤(h)=N(h)‚àímM(h)c(h)2.
œïm‚Ä≤‚Äã(h)=y‚Ä≤(h)‚àímx‚Ä≤(h)=c(h)2N(h)‚àímM(h)‚Äã.

At h=hbh=hb‚Äã, since M(hb)=0M(hb‚Äã)=0,
œïm‚Ä≤(hb)=N(hb)c(hb)2‚âÝ0.
œïm‚Ä≤‚Äã(hb‚Äã)=c(hb‚Äã)2N(hb‚Äã)‚ÄãÓÄÝ=0.

So for each fixed finite mm, œïm‚Ä≤œïm‚Ä≤‚Äã stays nonzero on a sufficiently small neighborhood UmUm‚Äã of hbhb‚Äã, hence œïmœïm‚Äã is strictly monotone there.

Because hbhb‚Äã is the common endpoint of the adjacent intervals and œïmœïm‚Äã is continuous and strictly monotone through hbhb‚Äã, the images on the two sides are ordered:
œïm(I1‚à©Um)‚à©œïm(I2‚à©Um)=‚àÖ,
œïm‚Äã(I1‚Äã‚à©Um‚Äã)‚à©œïm‚Äã(I2‚Äã‚à©Um‚Äã)=‚àÖ,

and the only common boundary point is œïm(hb)œïm‚Äã(hb‚Äã).

Since œïm‚Ä≤(hb)œïm‚Ä≤‚Äã(hb‚Äã) depends continuously on mm, the same statement holds uniformly for mm in any compact slope range.

That proves the theorem.

This is stronger than it looks.

It means the generic turning boundary is not merely ‚Äúlocally no-4-secant.‚Äù It is also locally no-support-overlap for every fixed finite slope. So the old adjacent-support theorem is already locally true there for a trivial reason:
œïm‚Ä≤(hb)‚âÝ0.
œïm‚Ä≤‚Äã(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0.

You do not need first-zero selection or the tangent kernel K(s,t)K(s,t) just to get the local ordering. The zero-capture machinery is only needed to push that local ordering out to the whole adjacent intervals.

There is also a clean vertical-line companion.
Vertical-line companion

meets neither adjacent interval in its interior, exactly as the current endpoint-tangent exclusion lemma already says.

So in fact every affine direction is locally support-ordered across a generic turning boundary:

    finite slopes by œïm‚Ä≤(hb)‚âÝ0œïm‚Ä≤‚Äã(hb‚Äã)ÓÄÝ=0,

    vertical slope by the strict extremum of xx.

That is a nice theorem, and it is genuinely new.
Why this helps the global proof

This meshes perfectly with the update you pasted.

The local finite-order W=0W=0 theorem says W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth. Your new theorem above says generic turning boundaries are locally sterile for support-overlap birth as well. So neither generic boundary type is where the bad configuration is born locally.

That leaves only a much narrower global problem:

    not local birth, but global persistence or transport of overlap/zero branches away from the boundary neighborhood.

And that is exactly where the current convo still locates the zero-capture issue.

So the next attack becomes cleaner.
The next exact reduction

    across a finite-order W=0W=0 boundary, the earlier determinant/divided-difference theorem shows a second opposite-side branch cannot be born locally.

So any global overlap

That suggests the next formal theorem to attack is this:
Adjacent-support reduction theorem

Let I1<I2I1‚Äã<I2‚Äã be adjacent generic intervals separated by a generic boundary (either turning or finite-order W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0). If

BI1‚Äã‚Äã(m)‚à©BI2‚Äã‚Äã(m)ÓÄÝ=‚àÖ

for some finite slope mm, then there exists an overlap point bb realized away from any boundary neighborhood.

That sounds modest, but it is exactly what you need: it converts the global overlap problem into an interior compact overlap problem, where first-zero / compactness arguments become legitimate.

And now the local theorems you already have justify the key truncation step that the old zero-capture route was missing morally but not formally:
the overlap cannot be ‚Äúborn at the boundary,‚Äù so if it exists, it exists in the interior after chopping off a small boundary neighborhood.

That is the sharpest way I know to continue the attack.
So the new plan is

    Keep the update‚Äôs split:

        direct q(7)q(7) witness survives,

        finite-order W=0W=0 is locally sterile,

        W‚â°0W‚â°0 intervals are excluded by the ŒªŒª-attack,

        remaining battlefield is turning-boundary continuation / zero-capture.

    Add the new generic turning-boundary support-ordering theorem above.

    Use the two local sterility theorems together to prove the adjacent-support reduction theorem: any genuine overlap must survive away from the boundary neighborhood.

    Only then re-enter the compact first-zero / tangency machinery on a genuinely interior compact box.

That last move is important. It makes the compact-first-zero step much more honest, because now the reason you can truncate away the boundary is not wishful ‚Äî it is backed by real local geometry on both boundary types.

So the exact next mathematical target is no longer ‚Äúprove adjacent sign-regularity globally.‚Äù It is:

    prove that any adjacent support overlap can be pushed off the boundary neighborhood onto a compact interior box.

Once that reduction is formalized, the old first-zero/tangency kernel becomes much more believable.

Not exactly.

They are very close, but they are different strengths.

The earlier target,
prove directly that BI1(m)‚à©BI2(m) has no interior overlap at all,
prove directly that BI1‚Äã‚Äã(m)‚à©BI2‚Äã‚Äã(m) has no interior overlap at all,

is a global adjacent-support theorem for that slope mm. If you proved that, you would already have the thing you really want for adjacent intervals: no same-slope line can hit both intervals in a ‚Äú2+2‚Äù way.

The later target,
if BI1(m)‚à©BI2(m)‚âÝ‚àÖ, then some overlap survives away from the boundary neighborhood,
if BI1‚Äã‚Äã(m)‚à©BI2‚Äã‚Äã(m)ÓÄÝ=‚àÖ, then some overlap survives away from the boundary neighborhood,

is weaker. It does not rule out overlap. It only says:

    local boundary geometry is not where the overlap is born,

    so any actual overlap must persist into an interior compact region,

    and therefore the compact first-zero / tangency machinery becomes applicable on that interior box.

So the relationship is:

    direct non-overlap theorem = stronger, final geometric statement;

    push-overlap-into-interior theorem = weaker reduction step that makes the old compact first-zero argument honest.

In logic:
direct non-overlap‚ÄÖ‚Ää‚üπ‚ÄÖ‚Ääpush-overlap-into-interior,
direct non-overlap‚üπpush-overlap-into-interior,

but not conversely.

Why I shifted to the weaker version is practical. You now have real local theorems on both boundary types:

    finite-order W=0W=0 boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth;

    generic turning boundaries are locally support-ordered.

Those are exactly the hypotheses you need for the weaker reduction. They do not yet seem strong enough by themselves to prove full global non-overlap immediately.

So the better next move is:

    prove local no-overlap near the boundary;

    deduce that any remaining overlap must occur away from the boundary;

    truncate to a compact interior box;

    then run first-zero / tangency on that box.

That is why the newer formulation is strategically better: it asks for less, but it may be enough to revive the existing endgame.

So the answer is: same direction, different strength. The ‚Äúpush overlap into a compact interior box‚Äù statement is the reduction step you can plausibly prove now; the ‚Äúno interior overlap at all‚Äù statement is the stronger theorem you would get only after finishing the rest.

Here is the reduction theorem.
Proposition: boundary-neighborhood truncation for adjacent pair-pair overlap

œïm(h):=y(h)‚àím‚Äâx(h),BI(m):=œïm(I).

Proof

There is a useful refinement.
Refinement: the tangency points for slope mm are also away from the boundary

At a generic turning boundary, the tangent slope is
m(h)=dy/dhdx/dh=N(h)M(h).

That means not only the secant intersections, but also the relevant tangency data for that fixed slope, live on compact interior pieces after removing a small boundary neighborhood.
What this buys you

This is exactly the weaker statement we were aiming for. It is not the full adjacent-support non-overlap theorem. It does not show

attack


Yes. Two things need correcting, and one thing needs to be weakened.

The main correction is the line

[
b\in \operatorname{int}\mathcal B_{I_i}(m)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
y=mx+b \text{ is 2-secant to }\Gamma(I_i).
]

That is **not true as stated**. It is only true when (m) lies in the **interior tangent-slope range** of (I_i). For a strictly convex graph, if (m) is outside that slope range, (\phi_m) can be monotone, (\mathcal B_I(m)) can still have interior, and an interior intercept can correspond to only one intersection. So the proposition should not use that equivalence bare. 

The second correction is in the conclusion. The proof only shows that after removing a small boundary neighborhood, there remains **at least one** point on each side with
[
\phi_m(h_i^\sharp)=b.
]
So what survives is **support overlap**
[
b\in \mathcal B_{J_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{J_2}(m),
]
not a full ‚Äúpair-pair overlap‚Äù or ‚Äú2-secant to both compact interiors.‚Äù To preserve actual pair-pair on the truncated interiors, you would need two surviving points on each side, and the current argument does not prove that. 

So the proposition is good, but it should be rewritten as a **support-overlap truncation** result, not a pair-pair truncation result.

The wording I would use is this:

[
\textbf{Corrected proposition.}
]

Let (I_1<I_2) be adjacent ECT intervals meeting at a generic turning boundary
[
c(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad M(h_b)=0,\qquad M'(h_b)\neq 0,\qquad N(h_b)\neq 0.
]
For a fixed finite slope (m), define
[
\phi_m(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)-m v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
\mathcal B_I(m):=\phi_m(I).
]

Assume either:

* (b\in \mathcal B_{I_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{I_2}(m)), if you only want support overlap, or
* the line (y=mx+b) is (2)-secant to both (\Gamma(I_1)) and (\Gamma(I_2)), if you want the stronger secancy hypothesis.

Then there exists a neighborhood (U) of (h_b) and compact subintervals
[
J_1\Subset I_1\setminus U,\qquad J_2\Subset I_2\setminus U
]
such that
[
b\in \mathcal B_{J_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{J_2}(m).
]

If you assume the stronger 2-secant hypothesis, the proof still only yields this support-overlap conclusion, not that (y=mx+b) remains (2)-secant to both (J_1) and (J_2). 

The proof then becomes clean:

since
[
\phi_m'(h_b)=\frac{N(h_b)}{c(h_b)^2}\neq 0,
]
after shrinking (U), (\phi_m) is strictly monotone on each one-sided piece
[
I_1\cap U,\qquad I_2\cap U.
]
So for each side, the equation (\phi_m(h)=b) has at most one solution in the boundary neighborhood. If there is at least one solution somewhere on that side to begin with, then at least one such solution survives in (I_i\setminus U). Taking small compact subintervals around those surviving points gives the conclusion. 

The refinement about tangency points being away from the boundary is fine. Since
[
m(h)=\frac{dy/dh}{dx/dh}=\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}
]
blows up one-sidedly at a generic turning boundary, no finite-slope tangency can occur arbitrarily close to (h_b). That part does not need correction. 

So the short verdict is:

* **correct:** local support-ordering at a generic turning boundary;
* **correct:** truncation of support overlap away from the boundary;
* **needs correction:** interior support value is not automatically equivalent to 2-secancy;
* **needs weakening:** the proof preserves support overlap on the truncated interiors, not full pair-pair.

That corrected version is still useful and is probably the right lemma to put before the compact first-zero machinery.

Yes ‚Äî your correction is right, and it changes the next move in a useful way.

The proposition should be a support-overlap truncation lemma, not a pair-pair truncation lemma. And the bad equivalence

b‚ààintBI‚Äã(m)‚ü∫y=mx+b is 2-secant to Œì(I)

should only be used when mm is in the interior tangent-slope range of II, exactly as you said. Corrected bridge theorem

    K21(s,t):=det‚Å°(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t)),K12(t,s):=det‚Å°(F(t),F‚Ä≤(t),F(s))

This is the right bridge, because your corrected truncation lemma only preserves support overlap. The way to get back to a kernel zero is to pass to an endpoint of the overlap interval, not to try to preserve full 2+22+2 secancy on the truncated compacts.

Here is the proof.

Because LL is 22-secant to Œì(Ii)Œì(Ii‚Äã), Rolle gives an interior point of IiIi‚Äã where the tangent slope equals mm. So mm lies in the interior tangent-slope range of each interval. Hence each branch has a unique interior tangent of slope mm, with tangent intercept
œÑIi(m)=inf‚Å°BIi(m).
œÑIi‚Äã‚Äã(m)=infBIi‚Äã‚Äã(m).

This is exactly the ‚Äúfixed-slope intercept‚Äù lemma already discussed in convo4.

Now use your corrected support-overlap truncation result. After deleting a sufficiently small boundary neighborhood UU, there exist compact subintervals
J1‚ãêI1‚àñU,J2‚ãêI2‚àñU
J1‚Äã‚ãêI1‚Äã‚àñU,J2‚Äã‚ãêI2‚Äã‚àñU

such that
b‚ààBJ1(m)‚à©BJ2(m).
b‚ààBJ1‚Äã‚Äã(m)‚à©BJ2‚Äã‚Äã(m).

Since finite-slope tangencies are also away from a generic turning boundary, we may enlarge JiJi‚Äã slightly if needed so that the unique slope-mm tangency point of each branch also lies in JiJi‚Äã. The refinement about tangencies being away from the boundary is valid because
m(h)=N(h)M(h)‚Üí¬±‚àû
m(h)=M(h)N(h)‚Äã‚Üí¬±‚àû

one-sidedly at a generic turning boundary.

Therefore each BJi(m)BJi‚Äã‚Äã(m) is a compact interval whose lower endpoint is the tangent intercept
œÑi:=œÑJi(m)=inf‚Å°BJi(m).
œÑi‚Äã:=œÑJi‚Äã‚Äã(m)=infBJi‚Äã‚Äã(m).

Now set
b‚àó:=inf‚Å°(BJ1(m)‚à©BJ2(m)).
b‚àó‚Äã:=inf(BJ1‚Äã‚Äã(m)‚à©BJ2‚Äã‚Äã(m)).

Because the two sets are compact intervals with nonempty intersection,
b‚àó=max‚Å°(œÑ1,œÑ2).
b‚àó‚Äã=max(œÑ1‚Äã,œÑ2‚Äã).

So b‚àób‚àó‚Äã is equal to one of the two tangent intercepts, and it lies in the support set of the other branch.

If b‚àó=œÑ2b‚àó‚Äã=œÑ2‚Äã, then the slope-mm tangent line to Œì(J2)Œì(J2‚Äã) meets Œì(J1)Œì(J1‚Äã). Thus there are interior points s‚ààJ2s‚ààJ2‚Äã, t‚ààJ1t‚ààJ1‚Äã with
det‚Å°(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t))=0,
det(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t))=0,

that is,
K21(s,t)=0.
K21‚Äã(s,t)=0.

If b‚àó=œÑ1b‚àó‚Äã=œÑ1‚Äã, then the slope-mm tangent line to Œì(J1)Œì(J1‚Äã) meets Œì(J2)Œì(J2‚Äã). Thus there are interior points t‚ààJ1t‚ààJ1‚Äã, s‚ààJ2s‚ààJ2‚Äã with
det‚Å°(F(t),F‚Ä≤(t),F(s))=0,
det(F(t),F‚Ä≤(t),F(s))=0,

that is,
K12(t,s)=0.
K12‚Äã(t,s)=0.

So any genuine adjacent pair-pair line yields a compact interior zero of one of the two directional tangent-separator kernels.

That is the corrected theorem.

This is better than trying to force the asymmetric kernel K21K21‚Äã immediately.

If you insist on producing specifically
K21(s,t)=0
K21‚Äã(s,t)=0

rather than ‚Äúone of K21,K12K21‚Äã,K12‚Äã,‚Äù then you need an extra orientation lemma proving that for the relevant slope mm,
œÑJ2(m)‚â•œÑJ1(m),
œÑJ2‚Äã‚Äã(m)‚â•œÑJ1‚Äã‚Äã(m),

so the lower endpoint of overlap must come from the right branch. But that is already very close to the full adjacent support-ordering theorem you were trying to prove, so it is too strong as an intermediate step.

The cleaner move is to symmetrize the first-zero/tangency machinery.

Instead of only proving a theorem for
K21(s,t)=det‚Å°(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t)),
K21‚Äã(s,t)=det(F(s),F‚Ä≤(s),F(t)),

prove the same compact first-zero / first-tangency statement for both directional kernels:
K21(s,t),K12(t,s).
K21‚Äã(s,t),K12‚Äã(t,s).

Then the corrected bridge above is enough: any adjacent pair-pair obstruction produces a compact interior zero of at least one directional kernel, and then the same first-zero/tangency contradiction can be run in whichever direction occurs.

So the attack now becomes:

    keep your corrected support-overlap truncation lemma;

    add the new overlap-endpoint ‚áí‚áí directional kernel zero lemma above;

    symmetrize the compact first-zero / first-adjacent-zero-implies-tangency argument.

That is the honest next hinge.

The reason this is such a good move is that it avoids smuggling the missing global orientation theorem back in through the side door. It uses exactly what your corrected proposition truly gives, and nothing stronger.

The shortest formulation of the next lemma would be:

    If a finite-slope line is 22-secant to both adjacent branches across a generic turning boundary, then after truncating away the boundary neighborhood there is a compact interior zero of one of the two directional tangent-separator kernels.

That is the statement I would try to freeze next.

\begin{proposition}[ECT intervals for the strengthened one-pair triple]

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{proposition}[Exclusion of $W$-flat intervals under direct septic nonvanishing]
\label{prop:no-W-flat-interval}
Assume that the direct $q^{(7)}$-driven slice of $\Delta_7(h)$ is
generically nonzero on the quintic-generic region. Let $J$ be a connected
open interval on which
\[
c(h)\neq 0,
\qquad
M(h)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
W\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Suppose for contradiction that
\[
W\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
By Proposition~\ref{prop:projective-wronskian-bridge},
\[
K_\Gamma(h)=\frac{W(h)}{c(h)^3}\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Since $M\neq 0$ on $J$, Proposition~\ref{prop:curvature-bridge-normalized-curve}
implies that
\[
\rho_2(h)=A\,\rho_1(h)+B
\]
for some constants $A,B\in\mathbf C$, i.e.
\[
\Delta_7(h)=A\,v_5(h)+B\,c(h)
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
This contradicts Proposition~\ref{prop:rho2-not-affine-in-rho1}. Therefore
$W$ cannot vanish identically on $J$.
\end{proof}

This is the clean theorem that captures the ŒªŒª-line‚Äôs reduced job.

\subsection{From the one-pair residual germ to two-pair and minimal-core rigidity}

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{theorem}[Finite-order $W=0$ boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth]
\label{thm:finite-order-w-zero-local-sterility}
Let $h_b$ satisfy
\[
c(h_b)\neq 0,
\qquad
M(h_b)\neq 0,
\qquad
W(h_b)=0,
\]
and assume that $W$ has finite vanishing order $r\ge 1$ at $h_b$:
\[
W(h)=(h-h_b)^r\,\widetilde W(h),
\qquad
\widetilde W(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
Define
\[
F(h):=(c(h),v_5(h),\Delta_7(h)),
\qquad
D(s,t,u):=\det(F(s),F(t),F(u)).
\]
Then, after shrinking to a sufficiently small neighborhood $U$ of $h_b$,
the following holds.

If $s<t<h_b$ lie in $U$, then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item if $r$ is even, the function $u\mapsto D(s,t,u)$ has no zero on the
opposite side $h_b<u\in U$;
\item if $r$ is odd, the function $u\mapsto D(s,t,u)$ has at most one zero on
the opposite side $h_b<u\in U$.
\end{enumerate}
The same conclusion holds with left and right exchanged. In particular, no
finite-order boundary of type $W=0,\ M\neq 0$ can support a local pair-pair
birth.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Work in the affine chart
\[
x(h):=\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
y(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}.
\]
Since
\[
x'(h)=\frac{M(h)}{c(h)^2},
\]
the hypothesis $M(h_b)\neq 0$ implies that $x$ is a valid local coordinate
near $h_b$. After translating so that $x(h_b)=0$ and subtracting the tangent
line, we may write the normalized curve as
\[
y=f(x),
\qquad
f(0)=f'(0)=0.
\]

By Proposition~\ref{prop:projective-wronskian-bridge},
\[
\frac{d^2y}{dx^2}=\frac{c(h)^3W(h)}{M(h)^3}.
\]
Because $x'(h_b)\neq 0$, the finite vanishing order of $W$ in $h$ is the same
as its finite vanishing order in the local coordinate $x$. Therefore
\[
f''(x)=\lambda x^r+O(x^{r+1})
\qquad(\lambda\neq 0).
\]

Fix two same-side points
\[
x_1<x_2<0
\]
sufficiently close to $0$, and define
\[
\widehat D(x_1,x_2,u):=
\det\!\begin{pmatrix}
1&x_1&f(x_1)\\
1&x_2&f(x_2)\\
1&u&f(u)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then
\[
\widehat D(x_1,x_2,u)
=
(x_2-x_1)(u-x_1)(u-x_2)\,H_{x_1,x_2}(u),
\]
where
\[
H_{x_1,x_2}(u):=f[x_1,x_2,u]
\]
is the second divided difference of $f$.

If $r$ is even, then $f''$ has fixed sign near $0$. By the Hermite--Genocchi
formula for second divided differences, $H_{x_1,x_2}(u)$ has that same fixed
sign for $u>0$ sufficiently small. Hence $\widehat D(x_1,x_2,u)\neq 0$ on the
opposite side.

If $r$ is odd, then
\[
f'''(x)=\lambda r\,x^{r-1}+O(x^r)
\]
has fixed nonzero sign near $0$, because $r-1$ is even. Differentiating with
respect to the repeated node gives
\[
\partial_u H_{x_1,x_2}(u)=f[x_1,x_2,u,u].
\]
By the Hermite--Genocchi formula for repeated-node divided differences,
$f[x_1,x_2,u,u]$ has the same fixed nonzero sign for $u>0$ sufficiently small.
Thus $u\mapsto H_{x_1,x_2}(u)$ is strictly monotone on the opposite side, and
therefore has at most one zero there.

Finally,
\[
D(s,t,u)=c(s)c(t)c(u)\,\widehat D(x(s),x(t),x(u)),
\]
and $c$ is nonzero on a small neighborhood of $h_b$, so the zero set of $D$
is exactly the zero set of $\widehat D$. The theorem follows.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Audit: residual $W=0$ pathology]
\label{rem:audit-residual-w0-pathology}
By Proposition~\ref{prop:no-W-flat-interval}, the $W=0,\ M\neq 0$ side is no
longer obstructed by open-interval flatness $W\equiv 0$ on a component with
$c\neq 0$ and $M\neq 0$. By
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-order-w-zero-local-sterility}, every finite-order
isolated $W=0$ boundary is locally sterile for pair-pair birth. Thus any
remaining $W=0$ issue would have to come either from non-analytic /
infinite-order flatness or from a genuinely global continuation phenomenon,
not from a generic local inflection birth mechanism.
\end{remark}

This is the big W=0W=0 cleanup theorem.

\begin{lemma}[Adjacent support-ordering]
\label{lem:adjacent-support-ordering}

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{lemma}[Support-overlap truncation across a generic turning boundary]
\label{lem:support-overlap-truncation-turning}
Let $I_1<I_2$ be adjacent ECT intervals meeting at a generic turning boundary
\[
c(h_b)\neq 0,
\qquad
M(h_b)=0,
\qquad
M'(h_b)\neq 0,
\qquad
N(h_b)\neq 0.
\]
For a fixed finite slope $m$, define
\[
\phi_m(h):=\frac{\Delta_7(h)-m v_5(h)}{c(h)},
\qquad
\mathcal B_I(m):=\phi_m(I).
\]
Assume
\[
b\in \mathcal B_{I_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{I_2}(m).
\]
Then there exists a neighborhood $U$ of $h_b$ and compact subintervals
\[
J_1\Subset I_1\setminus U,
\qquad
J_2\Subset I_2\setminus U
\]
such that
\[
b\in \mathcal B_{J_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{J_2}(m).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Differentiate:
\[
\phi_m'(h)=\frac{N(h)-mM(h)}{c(h)^2}.
\]
At $h=h_b$, since $M(h_b)=0$,
\[
\phi_m'(h_b)=\frac{N(h_b)}{c(h_b)^2}\neq 0.
\]
Hence for each fixed finite $m$, after shrinking to a small neighborhood $U$
of $h_b$, the function $\phi_m$ is strictly monotone on each one-sided piece
\[
I_1\cap U,
\qquad
I_2\cap U.
\]
Therefore, for each $i=1,2$, the equation
\[
\phi_m(h)=b
\]
has at most one solution in $I_i\cap U$.

But the assumption
\[
b\in \mathcal B_{I_i}(m)
\]
means exactly that there is at least one solution of $\phi_m(h)=b$ somewhere
on $I_i$. Therefore, after removing the boundary neighborhood $U$, at least
one such solution
\[
h_i^\sharp\in I_i\setminus U
\]
remains on each side. Choose small compact subintervals
\[
J_i\Subset I_i\setminus U
\]
with $h_i^\sharp\in J_i$. Then by continuity,
\[
b=\phi_m(h_i^\sharp)\in \phi_m(J_i)=\mathcal B_{J_i}(m),
\]
for $i=1,2$. This proves the claim.
\end{proof}

This is the corrected, weaker, and actually provable version.
4) Insert the directional-kernel bridge lemma

Where to insert

Insert this immediately after

\begin{lemma}[Support-overlap truncation across a generic turning boundary]
\label{lem:support-overlap-truncation-turning}
...
\end{lemma}

and before

\begin{lemma}[Adjacent support-ordering]
\label{lem:adjacent-support-ordering}

Insert this LaTeX

\begin{lemma}[Compact adjacent pair-pair implies a directional kernel zero]
\label{lem:pair-pair-gives-directional-kernel-zero}
Let $I_1<I_2$ be adjacent ECT intervals meeting at a generic turning boundary,
and let
\[
L:\ y=mx+b
\]
be a finite-slope line that is $2$-secant to both $\Gamma(I_1)$ and
$\Gamma(I_2)$.
Then, after removing a sufficiently small boundary neighborhood, there exist
compact subintervals
\[
J_1\Subset I_1,
\qquad
J_2\Subset I_2
\]
and points \(s\in J_2\), \(t\in J_1\) such that one of the two directional
kernels vanishes:
\[
K_{21}(s,t):=\det(F(s),F'(s),F(t))=0,
\]
or
\[
K_{12}(t,s):=\det(F(t),F'(t),F(s))=0,
\]
where
\[
F(h)=(c(h),v_5(h),\Delta_7(h)).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Because $L$ is $2$-secant to each branch, Lemma~\ref{lem:fixed-slope-intercept-sets}
shows that $m$ lies in the interior tangent-slope range of each interval.
Hence each branch has a unique interior tangent line of slope $m$, with tangent
intercept
\[
\tau_{I_i}(m)=\inf \mathcal B_{I_i}(m).
\]

At a generic turning boundary,
\[
\frac{dy/dh}{dx/dh}=\frac{N(h)}{M(h)}
\]
has one-sided blow-up, so no finite-slope tangency can occur arbitrarily close
to $h_b$. Therefore, after shrinking away a boundary neighborhood and applying
Lemma~\ref{lem:support-overlap-truncation-turning}, we may choose compact
subintervals
\[
J_1\Subset I_1,
\qquad
J_2\Subset I_2
\]
such that:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(b\in \mathcal B_{J_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{J_2}(m)\);
\item the unique slope-$m$ tangency point of each branch lies in the
corresponding \(J_i\).
\end{enumerate}
Hence each \(\mathcal B_{J_i}(m)\) is a compact interval whose lower endpoint
is the tangent intercept
\[
\tau_i:=\tau_{J_i}(m)=\inf \mathcal B_{J_i}(m).
\]

Now set
\[
b_*:=\inf\bigl(\mathcal B_{J_1}(m)\cap \mathcal B_{J_2}(m)\bigr).
\]
Since the intersection of two compact intervals is again a compact interval,
\[
b_*=\max(\tau_1,\tau_2).
\]
So \(b_*\) is equal to one of the two tangent intercepts, and it still lies in
the support set of the other branch.

If \(b_*=\tau_2\), then the slope-$m$ tangent line to \(\Gamma(J_2)\) meets
\(\Gamma(J_1)\). Thus there are points \(s\in J_2\), \(t\in J_1\) such that
\[
\det(F(s),F'(s),F(t))=0,
\]
i.e.
\[
K_{21}(s,t)=0.
\]

If \(b_*=\tau_1\), then the slope-$m$ tangent line to \(\Gamma(J_1)\) meets
\(\Gamma(J_2)\). Thus there are points \(t\in J_1\), \(s\in J_2\) such that
\[
\det(F(t),F'(t),F(s))=0,
\]
i.e.
\[
K_{12}(t,s)=0.
\]
This proves the lemma.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Audit: directional kernel orientation]
\label{rem:audit-directional-kernel-orientation}

one of \(K_{21},K_{12}\). The present reduction therefore moves the turning
problem from boundary-local geometry to compact directional-kernel geometry,
but does not yet identify a preferred direction.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Current state of the argument]
\label{rem:current-state-of-argument}
The local one-pair analysis now consists of three layers:
the cubic leading scalar $c(h)$, the quintic fixed-sector refinement
$A_5^{\mathfrak f}(h)$, and the septic determinant $\Delta_7(h)$.
These determine the normalized planar curve
\[
\Gamma(h)=\left(\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{\Delta_7(h)}{c(h)}\right),
\]
together with the derivative numerators
\[
M(h)=c(h)v_5'(h)-c'(h)v_5(h),
\qquad
N(h)=c(h)\Delta_7'(h)-c'(h)\Delta_7(h),
\]
and the projective Wronskian
\[
W(h)=
\det\!
\begin{pmatrix}
c&v_5&\Delta_7\\
c'&v_5'&\Delta_7'\\
c''&v_5''&\Delta_7''
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

On intervals where $c$, $M$, and $W$ do not vanish, the triple
$(c,v_5,\Delta_7)$ is an ECT system. Under the current direct septic
nonvanishing hypothesis, open-interval flatness $W\equiv 0$ is excluded on the
$c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0$ region by Proposition~\ref{prop:no-W-flat-interval}.
At isolated finite-order $W=0,\ M\neq 0$ boundaries,
Theorem~\ref{thm:finite-order-w-zero-local-sterility} shows that no local
pair-pair birth occurs.

across a generic turning boundary, then
Lemma~\ref{lem:pair-pair-gives-directional-kernel-zero} produces a compact
interior zero of one of the two directional kernels
\[
K_{21}(s,t)=\det(F(s),F'(s),F(t)),
\qquad
K_{12}(t,s)=\det(F(t),F'(t),F(s)).
\]

isolated in Remark~\ref{rem:audit-directional-kernel-orientation}.

first-order surjectivity, the quintic pure-value quotient detector, the full
order-$7$ fixed-sector algebra, and the turning-boundary directional-kernel
closure.
\end{remark}

latex
\begin{corollary}[No projective-Wronskian flatness on an \(M\neq 0\) region]
\label{cor:no-W-flatness-M-nonzero}
Assume that the direct \(q^{(7)}\)-driven slice of \(\Delta_7(h)\) is
generically nonzero on the quintic-generic region. Let \(J\) be a connected
open interval on which
\[
c(h)\neq 0,
\qquad
M(h)\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
W(h)\not\equiv 0
\]
on \(J\). Equivalently,
\[
K_\Gamma(h)\not\equiv 0
\]
on \(J\).
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Suppose \(W\equiv 0\) on \(J\). By
Proposition~\ref{prop:projective-wronskian-bridge},
\[
0=c(h)\,W(h)=M(h)N'(h)-N(h)M'(h)
\]
on \(J\). Since \(M(h)\neq 0\) on \(J\), it follows that
\[
\left(\frac{N}{M}\right)'=0,
\]
so
\[
\frac{N}{M}=A
\]
for some constant \(A\in\mathbf C\). By
Definition~\ref{def:MN-normalized-curve},
\[
\frac{\rho_2'}{\rho_1'}=\frac{N}{M}=A,
\]
hence
\[
\rho_2'=A\,\rho_1'.
\]
Integrating on the connected interval \(J\) gives
\[
\rho_2=A\,\rho_1+B
\]
for some constant \(B\in\mathbf C\). Equivalently,
\[
\Delta_7=A\,v_5+B\,c
\]
on \(J\), contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:rho2-not-affine-in-rho1}. Therefore \(W\not\equiv 0\) on
\(J\). The equivalent statement for \(K_\Gamma\) follows from
\(K_\Gamma=W/c^3\).
\end{proof}



Third, add a **short interpretive remark** right after that new corollary. This is the cleanest way to connect the Œª-line back to the direct septic slice without pretending the whole total pair ((u_7,v_7)) is closed.

latex
\begin{remark}[Interpretation of the \(\lambda\)-reduction]
\label{rem:lambda-reduction-no-W-flatness}
On the direct highest-new slice one has
\[
\Delta_7^{[1]}=\lambda^{[1]}v_5
\]
by Corollary~\ref{cor:direct-q7-septic-slice}. Thus if \(W\equiv 0\) on a
connected open interval with \(c\neq 0\) and \(M\neq 0\), then the affine
dependence
\[
\Delta_7=A\,v_5+B\,c
\]
forced in the proof above implies
\[
\Delta_7^{[1]}=A\,v_5,
\]
hence
\[
\lambda^{[1]}\equiv A
\]
on that interval. In this sense, the present argument excludes \(W\)-flatness
on an \(M\neq 0\) region without requiring a separate differential equation
for \(\lambda^{[1]}\); what remains open is the contribution of the
lower/mixed septic sectors to the full total pair \((u_7,v_7)\).
\end{remark}



I would also add one **audit remark**, but only if you want the draft to make the remaining caveat explicit. Put it immediately after the Œª-remark above. This is the honest boundary of what the Œª-line has actually achieved.

latex
\begin{remark}[Audit: no infinite-order \(W\)-flatness]
\label{rem:audit-no-infinite-order-W-flatness}
Corollary~\ref{cor:no-W-flatness-M-nonzero} excludes \(W\equiv 0\) on any open
interval with \(c\neq 0\) and \(M\neq 0\). To conclude that every
\(W=0,\ M\neq 0\) boundary is finite-order, one still needs the regularity
input that \(W\) is real-analytic on the relevant generic region. Once that is
recorded explicitly, infinite-order flatness is ruled out as well.
\end{remark}
