m1‚Äã>m2‚Äã,m3‚Äã>m2‚Äã,

but any line with intercept m=1m=1 is still on the 22-secant side of branches 11 and 33, while not being 22-secant to branch 22.

So from the current ingredients, you get local adjacent envelope separation, but not yet a monotone chain ordering.

That means the real remaining global theorem is now very sharply isolated:

    for each fixed bb, prove a global ordering / no-reentry theorem for the tangent-intercept functions mj(b)mj‚Äã(b).

Equivalently:

    either show the functions mj(b)mj‚Äã(b) cannot dip and then rise again as jj varies,

    or show the tangent locations Œºj(b)Œºj‚Äã(b) are ordered strongly enough that mj‚Ä≤(b)=‚àíŒºj(b)mj‚Ä≤‚Äã(b)=‚àíŒºj‚Äã(b) forces global ordering.

At this point, that theorem does not follow from what is already in the draft.

So the attack gives a mixed result:
What we gained

We reduced the whole remaining global geometry to a family of scalar envelope functions mj(b)mj‚Äã(b), and proved a strict adjacent separation theorem for them across generic turning boundaries.
What remains open

We still do not have a global no-reentry theorem for those envelopes.

And I think that is now the cleanest statement of the remaining gap.

So the honest ‚Äúattack result‚Äù is:

    the (Œº,Œª)(Œº,Œª)-reformulation is definitely the right language;

    the unconditional adjacent turning theorem translates into a strict adjacent ordering theorem for tangent envelopes;

    but the missing global step is now exactly:

    prove that the envelope family mj‚Äã(b) cannot re-enter globally.‚Äã

Based on this draft, can you give me a summary of everything we have learned since our current "zero-capture" targetted state

I‚Äôm pulling the current draft‚Äôs status/bottleneck sections and the new W=0W=0, directional-kernel, and turning-boundary theorem blocks so the summary matches what is actually in the paper now, not just our conversation memory.

Yes. Relative to the earlier ‚Äúzero-capture is the main target‚Äù state, the picture has changed a lot. The shortest honest summary is that we have learned the old bottleneck was too coarse: the draft is no longer just ‚Äústuck on zero-capture,‚Äù but has split the remaining work into a much smaller global propagation problem plus a shorter list of local algebraic audits.

What we learned first is that the W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 side is not a generic tangent-separator problem at all. In the normalized affine chart
x=v5c,y=Œî7c,
x=cv5‚Äã‚Äã,y=cŒî7‚Äã‚Äã,

a generic W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundary is an ordinary affine inflection, with cubic coefficient controlled by W‚Ä≤(hb)W‚Ä≤(hb‚Äã). So the old hope that the tangent-separator route would just extend across generic W=0W=0 boundaries was wrong; that route genuinely fails there. At the same time, the exact W/W‚Ä≤W/W‚Ä≤ identities show the obstruction is still encoded by the septic package through Œî7Œî7‚Äã, not by some new primitive order-9 invariant.

What we learned next is more positive: finite-order W=0, M‚âÝ0W=0, MÓÄÝ=0 boundaries are locally sterile for pair-pair birth. In graph language, they are just ordinary finite-order inflections, and the divided-difference analysis shows they cannot locally create the bad 2+22+2 line configuration. Paired with the no-WW-flatness result on M‚âÝ0MÓÄÝ=0 regions, that means the broad W=0W=0 side is no longer the main generic geometric obstruction. In practical terms: isolated finite-order W=0W=0 points are locally harmless, and open-interval W‚â°0W‚â°0 flatness is excluded under the septic non-affinity hypothesis.

On the turning-boundary side, the big advance is that we no longer need to treat ‚Äúadjacent pair-pair‚Äù as conditional on full zero-capture. The draft now has enough local turning geometry to prove an unconditional adjacent pair-pair exclusion across a generic turning boundary: strip exclusion against a compact opposite branch, compact first-contact, then tangency contradiction. So zero-capture is no longer the only game in town. There is still a stronger conditional directional-kernel route, but the actual adjacent 2+22+2 obstruction at a generic turning boundary has a direct closure now.

Another major lesson is that the determinant route is real, but subtler than first hoped. The three-point determinant
D(s,t,u)=det‚Å°(F(s),F(t),F(u))

does satisfy an exact mean-value / Peano-kernel formula in terms of the projective Wronskian WW. That gives genuine discrete sign-regularity on any interval where WW keeps one nonzero sign. But the naive hope that positivity of the kernel would automatically globalize the sign law across the whole chain turned out to be false. So the determinant route is not dead; it just reduces the global problem to a sharper object instead of solving it by itself.
